# Excalidraw Data

## Text Elements
QUANTITATIVE PERFORMANCE MODEL ^z4PCmkYX

Average Translation Cost\n─────────────────────────\nCost = Hit Rate × Hit Time\n     + Miss Rate × Miss Penalty\nTLB Hit Time:    ~1 cycle parallel with L1\nTLB Miss Penalty: N × DRAM latency\n                  ~60 to 200 ns per level\nTarget: Miss Rate below 1 percent\nfor typical workloads ^xn0SsrzC

ADDRESS TRANSLATION\n─────────────────────────\nHardware + OS Mechanism\nMaps Virtual Addresses used by programs\nto Physical Addresses in real DRAM\nWhile enforcing access protection ^Mq8InjDn

THREE CORE MOTIVATIONS\n─────────────────────────\n① Isolation: Each process has its own VA space\n   Same VA in Process A ≠ Same VA in Process B\n② Sharing: Multiple VAs can map to ONE PA\n   Used for shared libraries and IPC memory\n③ Protection: Access rights checked every translation\n   Read / Write / Execute / User vs Supervisor ^UC9n0UNn

VIRTUAL ADDRESS STRUCTURE\n─────────────────────────\nVirtual Address = VPN + Page Offset\nVPN  → Virtual Page Number\n      Identifies which virtual page\nOffset → Position within that page\n      IDENTICAL in VA and PA\nOnly VPN gets translated to PPN\nPage Offset passes through unchanged ^hhPZBjXX

MMU — Memory Management Unit\n─────────────────────────\nHardware unit on the CPU critical path\nSits BETWEEN 'generate address' and 'access memory'\nInput:  Virtual Address from CPU\nOutput: Physical Address for caches and DRAM\nAlso performs permission checks on EVERY access\nDefined in RISC-V Privileged ISA via satp CSR ^aW4zadg9

TLB — Translation Lookaside Buffer\n─────────────────────────\nSmall, fast, fully-associative cache INSIDE the CPU\nHolds recently used VPN → PPN mappings\nAvoids walking page tables on every access\nTypically 32 to 1024 entries\nSplit into iTLB and dTLB on modern CPUs\nFlushed on context switch unless ASID tagged ^BPeDvKML

TLB REACH\n─────────────────────────\nReach = Number of TLB Entries × Page Size\nExample: 64 entries × 4 KB = 256 KB reach\nIf working set exceeds reach → high miss rate\nLarger pages increase reach dramatically\nBut larger pages cause internal fragmentation\nHuge pages balance reach vs wasted space ^3hSCaD2L

PAGE TABLES\n─────────────────────────\nOS-defined data structures stored in DRAM\nMap every virtual page to a physical page frame\nStore permission bits: R W X Valid Dirty Accessed\nMulti-level to handle sparse 64-bit VA spaces\nSv39: 3 levels  →  PGD then PMD then PTE\nSv48: 4 levels  →  adds one more PGD level\nPOWER: Radix tree or Hashed Page Table option ^MoFEOS8d

TLB MISS PENALTY\n─────────────────────────\nHardware walker reads satp CSR for root table PA\nLevel 1: One DRAM read for PGD entry\nLevel 2: One DRAM read for PMD entry\nLevel 3: One DRAM read for PTE entry\nTotal: N DRAM reads for N-level page table\nThis is the primary latency of a TLB miss\nMore levels = more miss penalty on every miss ^ZLdaUWsi

PHYSICAL ADDRESS FORMATION\n─────────────────────────\nPA = PPN concatenated with Page Offset\nPPN comes from the Page Table Entry\nPage Offset is carried directly from VA\nThis concatenation is done in hardware\nPA is then used to access caches and DRAM\nNo arithmetic — just bit field replacement ^3QGVJrQD

VIRTUALLY INDEXED PHYSICALLY TAGGED Cache\n─────────────────────────\nKey insight: Offset bits are same in VA and PA\nCache INDEX uses offset bits from VA in parallel\nCache TAG uses Physical Address after translation\nThis hides TLB latency from L1 cache indexing\nMost modern L1 caches use this VIPT scheme\nExample: 4 KB page offset = 12 bits index the cache ^T3jCy2aY

SYNONYM AND ALIAS PROBLEM\n─────────────────────────\nSynonym: Two different VAs map to the SAME PA\nIf cache is virtually tagged, same data appears twice\nThis corrupts cache coherency and visibility\nSolution A: Use physically tagged caches always\nSolution B: OS enforces VA alignment constraints\nSolution C: Flush cache on alias creation ^ZUKt1KdB

IOMMU — Input Output MMU\n─────────────────────────\nSame concept applied to DMA-capable devices\nDevice issues IOVA — IO Virtual Address\nIOMMU translates IOVA to System Physical Address\nEnforces DMA protection like MMU enforces CPU access\nPrevents rogue devices from reading kernel memory\nRISC-V IOMMU spec defines this translation model ^wABOU2dt

TWO-STAGE TRANSLATION FOR VIRTUALIZATION\n─────────────────────────\nStage 1: Guest Virtual Address → Guest Physical Address\n  Controlled by Guest OS page tables\nStage 2: Guest Physical Address → Host Physical Address\n  Controlled by Hypervisor page tables\nBoth stages happen on every memory access in a VM\nEither stage can be set to Bare mode to disable it\nRISC-V IOMMU supports both stages natively ^BDPVtPSE

ISA ANCHOR POINTS\n─────────────────────────\nRISC-V: satp CSR controls Supervisor-mode translation\n  MODE field selects Bare, Sv39, Sv48, Sv57\n  PPN field holds root page table physical address\n  All S-mode instruction fetches implicitly read satp\nPOWER ISA: Radix tree and Hash page table modes\n  Both defined in OpenPOWER Foundation ISA spec\n  Hardware table walk vs software-managed TLB options ^ChNueTMG

Why does it exist? ^ZjCpBN2S

How are addresses structured? ^zL0RNWZw

Who does the translation? ^b0TQFdaE

How to avoid slow memory lookups? ^PZS3Q5Pi

What limits TLB effectiveness? ^HyOlLcu0

What if TLB does not hold the translation? ^tbOy2OaD

What is the cost of a miss? ^pSZ2TQ88

How is the Physical Address formed? ^qQudDKGz

How does cache interact with translation? ^w0fwfEkk

What alias problem exists? ^IZyMVx6n

How is translation extended to devices? ^MZzhqOOA

How does virtualization extend this? ^QnM4006o

What are the ISA-level controls? ^hDBMWkjy

governs performance via ^L2hhY8zy
